    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4774799991500403834">Echo Ridge is small-town America. Ellery's never been there, but she's heard all about it. Her aunt went missing there at age seventeen. And only five years ago, a homecoming queen put the town on the map when she was killed. Now Ellery has to move there to live with a grandmother she barely knows.<br/><br/>The town is picture-perfect, but it's hiding secrets. And before school even</span>
  <span id="freeText4774799991500403834" style="display:none">Echo Ridge is small-town America. Ellery's never been there, but she's heard all about it. Her aunt went missing there at age seventeen. And only five years ago, a homecoming queen put the town on the map when she was killed. Now Ellery has to move there to live with a grandmother she barely knows.<br /><br />The town is picture-perfect, but it's hiding secrets. And before school even begins for Ellery, someone's declared open season on homecoming, promising to make it as dangerous as it was five years ago. Then, almost as if to prove it, another girl goes missing.<br /><br />Ellery knows all about secrets. Her mother has them; her grandmother does too. And the longer she's in Echo Ridge, the clearer it becomes that everyone there is hiding something. The thing is, secrets are dangerous--and most people aren't good at keeping them. Which is why in Echo Ridge, it's safest to keep your secrets to yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4774799991500403834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4870494-kristia-seabolt"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1588768470i/4870494._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4870494-kristia-seabolt">Kristia Seabolt</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    He was a vindictive, egotistical monster, and didn't take Sadie's rejection well at all, so he wanted revenge, or he tried to force himself onto "Sadi<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    He was a vindictive, egotistical monster, and didn't take Sadie's rejection well at all, so he wanted revenge, or he tried to force himself onto "Sadie" when it was Sarah. When Sarah rejected him as well, he must have gotten angry and lashed out and killed her (either intentionally or unintentionally), and thus gave him his lust for young, homecoming Queen girls, and the tendency of killing them. The reason Ellery didn't say anything to anyone for Peter doing this, even when his answer was a confession, "I thought she was your mother.", she didn't want to devastate her family and mostly her mother, for fear of her backsliding in her recovery, and this feeling even more guilty for her sister's death. Ellery figured it would cause more damage than mending at this point. Although it's a pity that they won't know what he did with her body or how he killed her, he'd most likely not confessed to it anyways.<br />As the book ended on the note, some things are best left unsaid.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The original quote the title is based on (and the theme song for Pretty Little Liars) is "Three may keep a secret, if two of them are dead," by Benjam<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The original quote the title is based on (and the theme song for Pretty Little Liars) is "Three may keep a secret, if two of them are dead," by Benjamin Franklin. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_750').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4156895001186217889"><i>"If I believed in omens, this would be a bad one."</i><br/><br/>This is a difficult review to write, as I was so taken with McManus's debut last year, but as an adult reader I didn't feel her sophomore effort lived up to the hype I had created in my head. Obviously this is no one's fault but my own, and as a novel for YA readers I think it will be well received as it still gives off a similar vibe as <i>One Of Us Is Lying</i>, although I found this one to be much slower paced and less twisty than her previous work. </span>
  <span id="freeText4156895001186217889" style="display:none"><i>"If I believed in omens, this would be a bad one."</i><br /><br />This is a difficult review to write, as I was so taken with McManus's debut last year, but as an adult reader I didn't feel her sophomore effort lived up to the hype I had created in my head. Obviously this is no one's fault but my own, and as a novel for YA readers I think it will be well received as it still gives off a similar vibe as <i>One Of Us Is Lying</i>, although I found this one to be much slower paced and less twisty than her previous work. Personally, this was more of a 2-2.5 star read, but I feel the YA audience will feel this is an overall positive experience and the final twist in the last line of the book will blow a good number of readers out of the water. <br /><br />----------<br /><br />Beyond thrilled to announce that this is our #ScaredSuspenseBookClub pick for January 2019! If you'd like to join in with our discussions, please follow our new account over on Instagram, @scaredsuspensebookclub. &lt;3</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2707802390" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2707802390?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2707802390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3650737784049175356">3.5 Stars! This was a fair and enjoyable read.I have no intentions of picking up <i>One Of Us Is Lying</i>, but I decided to give <i>Two Can Keep A Secret</i> a chance. It was not the most notable young adult thriller on the market, but I enjoyed my time reading. <br/><br/>CW: murder, grief, talk of substance abuse, statutory rape<br/><br/>If any other readers happen to be confused if they must read Karen M. McManus’s first novel to understand her second (as I initially was), you don’t! They’re totally separate stories. As I hav</span>
  <span id="freeText3650737784049175356" style="display:none">3.5 Stars! This was a fair and enjoyable read.I have no intentions of picking up <i>One Of Us Is Lying</i>, but I decided to give <i>Two Can Keep A Secret</i> a chance. It was not the most notable young adult thriller on the market, but I enjoyed my time reading. <br /><br />CW: murder, grief, talk of substance abuse, statutory rape<br /><br />If any other readers happen to be confused if they must read Karen M. McManus’s first novel to understand her second (as I initially was), you don’t! They’re totally separate stories. As I have not read <i>One Of Us Is Lying</i>, I can’t exactly compare the two. Based off of reviews, what I can say is that <i>Two Can Keep A Secret</i> seems to have made great improvements in terms of representation. I was surprised to find out the main twins are latinx (one of them being gay) and there are two Asian side characters (one being bisexual). I can’t say for sure, but it seems as if the author made deliberate improvements in creating characters free from stereotypes and I was pleased to see this inclusion.<br /><br />I did enjoy the writing of this book. It’s not super flowery or dense and was easy to devour. One issue I did pick up on is the novel was VERY repetitive. I feel like every chapter, we were given a recap on what had happened in the past and how it ties into what is going on in the present. I just did not need a constant summary of the girls who had gone missing in past years and it did weigh down the book at times.<br /><br /><br />The characters were fine, but nothing special. I actually think each person would have benefitted from more development, as I can’t say much about them beyond their role in the story. The mystery was alright, but the majority of the novel didn’t WOW me. I was shocked by the final reveal, which is a plus because I’ve been fairly underwhelmed with some of the thrillers I have read recently. The END END of the novel was also super unexpected. It left a lasting, chilling impression I was not prepared for.<br /><br /><i>Two Can Keep A Secret</i> isn’t at the top of my favorites list and there are distinct problems I had with it, but I overall really enjoyed my time reading this book and am definitely happy I spent my time on it. If you’re looking for the most amazing thriller to ever grace bookshelves, this ain’t it. But if you just want a simple mystery thriller to have fun with, I think it’s worth the read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3650737784049175356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2670691426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2670691426" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2670691426?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141375656" href="/book/show/40099425-two-can-keep-a-secret">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2670691426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17836029625273652183">the saying goes that ‘two can keep a secret if one of them is dead,’ but what isnt mentioned is that secrets like to be shared. its in their very nature and karen mcmanus definitely understands that. this book is full of secrets just dying to get out!<br/><br/>and whilst i didnt think this was quite as good as <i>‘one of us is lying,’</i> it definitely does not feel like a sophomore slump of a novel. its fast-paced, clever, and downright mysterious. i actually didnt find this to be predicable, which is the case </span>
  <span id="freeText17836029625273652183" style="display:none">the saying goes that ‘two can keep a secret if one of them is dead,’ but what isnt mentioned is that secrets like to be shared. its in their very nature and karen mcmanus definitely understands that. this book is full of secrets just dying to get out!<br /><br />and whilst i didnt think this was quite as good as <i>‘one of us is lying,’</i> it definitely does not feel like a sophomore slump of a novel. its fast-paced, clever, and downright mysterious. i actually didnt find this to be predicable, which is the case with most YA thrillers, so that was exciting for me. i enjoyed how my opinion of everyone and everything constantly changed as the story progressed, and i think thats a sign of good storytelling. <br /><br />and really, the only issue i have is with some particular writing style choices that made the story feel a bit disjointed. for example, a chapter ends right in the middle of a scene/situation. the reader is then told what occurs next through little introspective flashbacks via a main character in the next chapter, which happens to begin halfway through the day after said scene/situation. this happens consistently - its just a weird way of telling a story to me and not really beneficial in any way. i feel like a much more consecutive storytelling method would have been more effective.<br /><br />regardless of my nit-picking, i really did enjoy the book. its entertaining, discreet, and everything i would expect from KM. if you enjoyed <i>‘one of us is lying,’</i> then you really need to pick this up ASAP! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17836029625273652183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3488720654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3488720654" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3488720654?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141375656" href="/book/show/40099425-two-can-keep-a-secret">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3488720654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12756912563397463679"><i>”Missing girls don’t come home in Echo Ridge, Ryan,” she says in a hollow voice. “You know that.”</i><br/><br/>Okay, to read Courtney Summer’s <b>“Sadie”</b> at the same time as <b>“Two Can Keep a Secret”</b> was <s>probably</s> definitely not one of my best ideas but thankfully those two books went into two completely different directions and this is probably the only reason why I was able to continue with both. XD The story in here went in the direction of a good “Whodunit?” though, and kept me thinking while I tried to put all</span>
  <span id="freeText12756912563397463679" style="display:none"><i>”Missing girls don’t come home in Echo Ridge, Ryan,” she says in a hollow voice. “You know that.”</i><br /><br />Okay, to read Courtney Summer’s <b>“Sadie”</b> at the same time as <b>“Two Can Keep a Secret”</b> was <s>probably</s> definitely not one of my best ideas but thankfully those two books went into two completely different directions and this is probably the only reason why I was able to continue with both. XD The story in here went in the direction of a good “Whodunit?” though, and kept me thinking while I tried to put all the puzzle pieces into their right place. And yes, I solved the mystery when I was about halfway through the book but that didn’t take away any of my enjoyment. On the contrary, it was pretty satisfying to see it all unfold and to know I was right. *lol* I’m just weird like that. ;-P<br /><br /><i>”I finally meet his eyes full-on. They’re sad and scared and, yes, kind. In that moment, I choose to believe he’s not a Kelly boy with a temper, or someone with opportunity and motive, or the quiet kind you’d never suspect, I choose to believe he’s the person he’s always shown himself to be.<br />I choose to trust him.”</i><br /><br />One of the things I enjoyed the most about “Two Can Keep a Secret” was the characters and their friendships. McManus always makes them very relatable and her concept of a bad boy and a clever girl seems to be some sort of trademark. At least Mal and Ellery definitely fit that bill. As did Nate and Bronwyn in <b>“One of Us is Lying”</b>. It is also always those two characters who try to solve the mystery in the end. ;-) Still, it’s a nice concept and it works, even though I’ve to admit that I wish some of the other characters would have been more fleshed out. Don’t get me wrong, Ellery and especially Malcom were interesting lead characters, but I really wish we would have gotten to see more of Mia and Ezra. I mean Mia is Mal’s best friend and Ezra is Ellery’s twin. You’d think they would have been a more active part of the book, but in fact they were just side characters that were never part of the big action. <br /><br /><i>”If I weren’t so sick to my stomach, I might laugh at how fiercely Mia glares at everyone we pass in the hallway. “Go ahead and try it,” she mutters, as a couple of Kyle’s teammates who are twice her size give me the once-over. “I hope you do.”</i><br /><br />This is me counting beans though so I’m pretty sure others won’t see this as a flaw. The setting of the small town Echo Ridge and its amusement park made for a really great atmosphere and I’ve to admit that I loved all the little details and secrets that weren’t a part of the bigger plot but still played a part in the general scheme of things. XD I know that sounded pretty vague now but just like with “One of Us is Lying” I don’t want to spoil any of the fun and want you to experience this for yourself. ;-P<br /><br />All told <b>“Two Can Keep a Secret”</b> was a really nice murder mystery that was entertaining and not all too heavy to read. Sure, the topic of missing girls and dead homecoming queens is a tough one by nature, the balance between serious subjects and enjoyable moments was nicely done though. So if you feel like reading a light “Whodunit?” that will keep you guessing this might turn out to be the right book for you. =)<br /><br />_________________________________<br /><br />This was really good even though I managed to solve the mystery but then again that was a huge part of the fun! *lol*<br />Malcom was such a precious snowflake and I loved his friendship with Mia! &lt;3<br />Thankfully this was not as serious as “Sadie” and I could continue to read both books. McManus definitely has a talent to keep you guessing. ;-)<br /><br />Full RTC soon! Stay tuned!<br />__________________________________<br /><br />It’s time to broaden my horizon again and to read another mystery book!<br />I loved <b>“One of Us is Lying”</b> so I’m really looking forward to read <b>“Two Can Keep A Secret”</b>, which automatically remembers me of the title song of “Pretty Little Liars”. *lol*<br /><br />Let’s hope the sentence doesn’t end like the lyrics in the song.... “Two can keep a secret if one of them is dead.” &gt;_&lt;<br /><br />Then again this book seems to be about murdered Homecoming Queens so yeah, <i>“if one of them is dead”</i> might actually be the right assumption. XD<br /><br />Let’s stop pondering and find out instead! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12756912563397463679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2684357018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2684357018" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2684357018?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141375656" href="/book/show/40099425-two-can-keep-a-secret">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=thriller-crime">thriller-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2684357018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4685583894906157801"><b>Ok so this was EXCELLENT and exactly what I want a thriller to be!</b> Usually I'm tentative about thrillers and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32571395.One_of_Us_Is_Lying' title='One of Us Is Lying by Karen M. McManus' rel='nofollow noopener'>One of Us Is Lying</a>, while I admire it for being super-famous, it didn't click so much for me. However this one?! Miiiiine. It had the small town vibes, an autumn-y Halloween aesthetic, siblings dynamics, took time to develop the characters, and it had muuuuurder. Obviously. It is literally a murder mystery. But someone must be Captain McObvious here and I volunteer.<br/><br/>anyway.<br/><br/><b> ➸ I really care</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4685583894906157801" style="display:none"><b>Ok so this was EXCELLENT and exactly what I want a thriller to be!</b> Usually I'm tentative about thrillers and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32571395.One_of_Us_Is_Lying" title="One of Us Is Lying by Karen M. McManus" rel="nofollow noopener">One of Us Is Lying</a>, while I admire it for being super-famous, it didn't click so much for me. However this one?! Miiiiine. It had the small town vibes, an autumn-y Halloween aesthetic, siblings dynamics, took time to develop the characters, and it had muuuuurder. Obviously. It is literally a murder mystery. But someone must be Captain McObvious here and I volunteer.<br /><br />anyway.<br /><br /><b> ➸ I really cared about the characters!</b><br />That's what I want out of a book, ok!? Make me CARE. (Which is hard with my stone cold little rock of a heart.) But the book balanced developing the twisty murder mystery AND developing both the narrators (Ellery and Malcolm) into dimensional and complex humans who need a hug several times during the course of the book. Or two hugs, in Malcolm's case. Kid had it rough.<br /><br />✧<b>Ellery:</b> So she just moved to Echo Ridge (while her mum is in rehab) and she and her twin brother, Ezra, are staying with their estranged grandma. Ellery has a bushel of curly hair, possibly Latinx complexion (unsure of her dad), and a deep love of murder mysteries. Her brother is the chill sweetheart who frequently has to say things like: "NO MURDER BEFORE BREAKFAST ELLERY." And I loved them so much. (I wish Ezra had been more developed though. He's queer, but he's just a sliver of the storyline so.)<br />✧ <b>Malcolm:</b> Ok so his older brother is the aggressive angry jock dude, who was heavily suspected in his girlfriend's murder several years ago. Never arrested though. But Malcolm lives in that shadow, despite his mum having remarried this rich flashy lawyer and now Malcolm's actual step-sister is like the QUEEN BEE of highschool. But anyway. Malcolm is a little nerdy and dorky and Soft™. I absolutely adore how his relationship with Ellery was really slowburn, despite the shortness of the book. <br /><br />I lowkey suspected him of murder at one point but like ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ I SUSPECTED EVERYONE. SUREFIRE WAY TO BE RIGHT AT THE END.<br /><br /><b>➸ The plot had me super invested.</b><br />I think because I cared about the characters so easily? But I wanted to know if these string of missing-girls was connected. It reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34810320.Sadie" title="Sadie by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Sadie</a> a bit, when they called out how missing girls need to be taken seriously, not just called a statistic. It's twisty and there's lots of theories with Ellery playing detective (but she's not obnoxious about it). I called one of the twists about her mother's past! I'M PRACTICALLY SHERLOCK. Nevermind that I was lmao so wrong about the murderer. Anyway.<br /><br />➸ <b>I do confess the amount of characters had me afloat down a river with just a paddle-pop stick to cling to.</b><br />There were so. many. names. I forget my own name frequently and have been known to collectively refer to my nephews as Frank because *waves vaguely* too many. help me. Occasionally they'd throw in a name and I'd be like: WHO. But otherwise, I did ok! I think! Especially when everyone had like super common names (LIZ, SARAH, MIA, DAISY, BROOKE, OH GOD).<br /><br /><b>➸ It was really satisfying.</b><br />I just enjoyed myself ok?! I had a thoroughly good time reading this and ok ok it wasn't the wildest mystery every. My heart didn't bust out of my chest. But it felt like a sinister contemporary, full of autumn leaves and family secrets, with a background of murderrrr. Perfect for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4685583894906157801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2432143053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2432143053" />
    <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks"><img alt="BernLuvsBooks " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585010050p2/3087404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2432143053?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2432143053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10866063316758266274"><b>4 I Didn't See That Coming Stars</b><br/><br/>Ellery and her twin brother arrive at their mother's hometown of Echo Ridge in a hail storm to discover a body on the road - a local high school teacher victim of a hit and run. That welcome was merely the beginning. The twins quickly find their new home is seeped in secrets, disappearing girls and murder. It all began with the disappearance of their mother's twin sister on Homecoming Night. Her disappearance may have remained unsolved but its effects ran deep bot</span>
  <span id="freeText10866063316758266274" style="display:none"><b>4 I Didn't See That Coming Stars</b><br /><br />Ellery and her twin brother arrive at their mother's hometown of Echo Ridge in a hail storm to discover a body on the road - a local high school teacher victim of a hit and run. That welcome was merely the beginning. The twins quickly find their new home is seeped in secrets, disappearing girls and murder. It all began with the disappearance of their mother's twin sister on Homecoming Night. Her disappearance may have remained unsolved but its effects ran deep both within their family and the community at large. <br /><br />Fast forward 5 years and another Homecoming Queen, Lacey goes missing and ends up dead. Now, the twins find themselves in the middle of yet another mystery when the town in besieged with bloody messages, broken dolls and other ominous threats to members of the current Homecoming Court. <i>
  <b>Are all these events related? What evil lurks in Echo Ridge?</b>
</i><br /><br />I was a huge fan of McManus' first book, <u>One of Us is Lying</u> so I had high expectations for her second novel. While I found this one engaging I definitely wasn't as blown away as I was with the first book. Still, it was a fun read. Echo Ridge and its inhabitants were interesting, creepy and felt like a guilty pleasure to read about. It seems like everyone had some skeletons hidden in their closet which added to the <i>whodunnit</i> aspect. I kept going round and round, changing my mind on who the "bad guy" was and speculating on their motive. I was a bit underwhelmed by the reveal but I think I just wanted/expected a bit more after <u>One of Us is Lying</u>. My mind had certainly come up with a few outlandish theories that I was hoping would be correct! <br /><br />All in all, a strong sophomore effort by Karen McManus. I look forward to seeing what else she comes up with. Keep it BIG Karen - you know how to do that well!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10866063316758266274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2441042713" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2441042713" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2441042713?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2441042713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9366833426635246286">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>With <b>
  <i>Two Can Keep a Secret</i>
</b>, her follow-up to the excellent <b>
  <i>One of Us is Lying</i>
</b> (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2019039414' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>see my review</a>), Karen M. McManus proves she's not a flash-in-the-pan talent, but rather a pretty terrific storyteller, one who is tremendously skilled at depicting the complex behaviors of teenagers, and the mysteries that unfold in front of our eyes.<br/><br/>Ellery and her twin brother Ezra have to leave their California home and move to Echo Ridge, a small town in Vermont, and live with their maternal grand</span>
  <span id="freeText9366833426635246286" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />With <b>
  <i>Two Can Keep a Secret</i>
</b>, her follow-up to the excellent <b>
  <i>One of Us is Lying</i>
</b> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2019039414" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">see my review</a>), Karen M. McManus proves she's not a flash-in-the-pan talent, but rather a pretty terrific storyteller, one who is tremendously skilled at depicting the complex behaviors of teenagers, and the mysteries that unfold in front of our eyes.<br /><br />Ellery and her twin brother Ezra have to leave their California home and move to Echo Ridge, a small town in Vermont, and live with their maternal grandmother while their mother goes to rehab. They've never been to Echo Ridge before, and barely know their grandmother, despite the fact that their mother grew up there, and was even crowned homecoming queen. But that night, their aunt (their mother's twin sister) disappeared and was never seen or heard from again.<br /><br />Their aunt's disappearance wasn't the town's only tragedy. Five years ago, Lacey Kilduff was crowned homecoming queen and was then found murdered shortly thereafter. It's a crime that affected many in Echo Ridge, as the murder was never solved, yet many town residents have their suspicions about who is guilty, and they take it out on anyone connected to him.<br /><br />"'I should probably preface this by saying...I think about crime a lot. Like, an abnormal amount. I get that. It's sort of a problem. So you have to take what I say with a grain of salt, because I'm just this...naturally suspicious person, I guess.'"<br /><br />For someone fairly obsessed with true crime, a town with as many secrets as Echo Ridge is a treasure trove for Ellery. Not only does she want to understand what happened to her aunt Sarah all those years ago (not to mention why her mother has kept them from Echo Ridge), but she begins finding clues to what might have happened to Lacey. And when it appears that someone is threatening to harm another candidate for homecoming queen, Ellery is determined to uncover all of the answers—but it may put her own life in danger in the process, because someone wants to keep the town's secrets hidden.<br /><br />Just like anytime I read a book that has any type of mystery component, I'm immediately suspicious of <i>everyone</i>. A new character shows up? Bam, they're a suspect. The funny thing is, McManus really did keep me guessing here, and while I wasn't shocked with how things resolved themselves, I wasn't disappointed either. There definitely were some good twists to be had here, and McManus gave you characters to root for and characters to instantly dislike. (And here's a funny point—this is the third book I've read in the last year with a main character named Ellery.)<br /><br />A hallmark of YA books is characters that are more articulate and sarcastic than most adults, and while that's certainly the case with the characters in <b>
  <i>Two Can Keep a Secret</i>
</b>, it felt right here and didn't detract from how much I liked this. I also liked the way diversity was presented as almost an afterthought—there was too much going on in the high school and around town for anyone to focus on someone's sexuality or ethnicity. (I would have liked a same-sex relationship thrown in, but I know that wasn't the focus of the story.)<br /><br />As far as I'm concerned, McManus is now two for two, and seeing as I started this book the day after it was released, I'll probably have a while to wait until her next book. I'm sure it will be worth the wait, but until then, I love marveling at the incredible depth and breadth of talented writers creating such fantastic YA books these days. <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>, or check out my list of the best books I read in 2018 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9366833426635246286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=sisters">sisters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=contemporary-recent">contemporary-recent</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=alcoholism-drugs">alcoholism-drugs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2510404820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13839314113822155247"><i> All of Fright Farm's success is based on how much people love to be scared in a controlled environment. There's something deeply satisfying about confronting a monster and escaping unscathed. Real monsters aren't anything like that. They don't let go." </i><br/><br/>3.5 ⭐️<br/><br/>I did enjoy Karen McManus' second novel, but it didn't blow me away as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32887579.One_of_Us_is_Lying' title='One of Us is Lying by Karen M. McManus' rel='nofollow noopener'>One of Us is Lying</a> did.<br/><br/>Ellery and Ezra have moved to their mother's home town of Echo Ridge with their grandmother, while their mum is in rehab. Echo Ridge is fa</span>
  <span id="freeText13839314113822155247" style="display:none"><i> All of Fright Farm's success is based on how much people love to be scared in a controlled environment. There's something deeply satisfying about confronting a monster and escaping unscathed. Real monsters aren't anything like that. They don't let go." </i><br /><br />3.5 ⭐️<br /><br />I did enjoy Karen McManus' second novel, but it didn't blow me away as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32887579.One_of_Us_is_Lying" title="One of Us is Lying by Karen M. McManus" rel="nofollow noopener">One of Us is Lying</a> did.<br /><br />Ellery and Ezra have moved to their mother's home town of Echo Ridge with their grandmother, while their mum is in rehab. Echo Ridge is famous for its Homecoming Queen murder. Lacey, a few years older than the twins was murdered in the fair ground then known as <i>Murderland</i> before it changed its name.<br />Before that, when their mother was in school, her twin sister disappeared, but was never found.<br /><br />Now it seems the Murderland Killer is back. There is graffiti everywhere with threats; who is behind them and why? And when another girl going missing - things are looking grim.<br /><br />When Ellery is one of the targeted homecoming Queens, tensions are high. I liked that the plot kept me guessing, and that we had no idea who could have been behind it. I was pleased with the final reveal. The only part I didn't like much was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[we are told that Sarah (Ellery and Ezra's Aunt) was killed mistakenly, because the killer thought she was her twin sister Sadie. But 1. how does a killer not know who he is killing? And 2. Why did he want to kill Sadie in the first place? The other girls are killed because he was sleeping with them and they were going to blab. Is this the same case for Sadie? As it is never entirely explained. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, entertaining enough. Just not enough lovable characters as One of Us is Lying, and a few loose ends I felt needed tying up, just not as polished I thought.</span>

I was hyped and my expectations were huge. Silly me. Maybe if I hadn't psyched myself up so much I wouldn't feel so severely disappointed as I do right now. <br/><br/><br/>Ellery and her twin brother, Ezra, are sent to stay with their grandmother, in Echo Ridge, while their mom is in rehab for treatment.   <span id="freeText7298790243497692060" style="display:none">When I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2651701514?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">One of Us Is Lying</a> I immediately wanted to get my hands on Karen McManus's next book. Ellery is curious about this town that their mother hardly speaks about. The town where her own twin sister went missing right after prom. It is also a town where just five years ago another girl was murdered on prom night. <br><br>Strange things happen in Echo Ridge, but it just so happens that Ellery is a crime book fanatic. And ever since the night of their arrival weird things start happening once again.<br><br><br>I didn't feel any sort of attachment to the characters. Besides Malcom, he I liked. And it's sad because that is what I really loved about McManus's last book. I loved those characters and it was what made the book great for me. <br><br>The mystery of this book was very luke warm.   <span id="freeText481087398603220532" style="display:none">Here's the thing: I'm not necessarily the biggest fan of YA thrillers as an overall genre, but there's something about Karen McManus's work that pulls me in and keeps me frantically flipping pages until the end. <div id="review_2710502318" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2710502318" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2710502318?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=2019-publications">2019-publications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2710502318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5098803904932986056">Overall, I found this much less eye-roll-worthy than ONE OF US IS LYING. The author still is too much in love with stereotypes… I mean, homecoming queens dying? Please. But I felt more engaged somehow with only two narrators, a boy and a girl (Ellery and Malcolm), love interests to each other and both involving themselves in the mystery case(s). Both are likeable and smart(ish) leads. Actually, anything I say about one of them basically immediately applies to the other because, frankly, they hav</span>
  <span id="freeText5098803904932986056" style="display:none">Overall, I found this much less eye-roll-worthy than ONE OF US IS LYING. The author still is too much in love with stereotypes… I mean, homecoming queens dying? Please. But I felt more engaged somehow with only two narrators, a boy and a girl (Ellery and Malcolm), love interests to each other and both involving themselves in the mystery case(s). Both are likeable and smart(ish) leads. Actually, anything I say about one of them basically immediately applies to the other because, frankly, they have such similar voices it’s hard at times to distinguish them. <br /><br />The twin element was smart. There’s a very direct link to it in the very last sentence of this book, which gave me shivers. WOAH. That’s one of the best last sentences I’ve ever read. Out of context, it’s heh. But because of everything that happens, it’s just perfectly placed and perfectly creepy. At times, this book will give you A SIMPLE FAVOR vibes. (Anyone watched the movie?). I feared the author would parallel the two stories a little too much to stay on her own course and not end up using ideas from that one, but fortunately that never happened. Thank God. I didn’t see anything coming. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5098803904932986056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2467957158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2467957158" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2467957158?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781984829085" href="/book/show/40567288-two-can-keep-a-secret">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=at-home-reading">at-home-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2467957158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14278002562603967701">This book has fallen victim to the “Loved the last book so I had high expectations” syndrome. I thought One of Us Is Lying was great, Two Can Keep a Secret was just okay.<br/><br/>I expect these books to be cheesy – but this one was maybe too cheesy.<br/><br/>The dialogue and the characters once again reminded me of a CW TV show. The blurb on the book does mention Riverdale and during the book one of the characters even mentions all the male actors on the CW. I think all of this combined felt like, “Look at me! I a</span>
  <span id="freeText14278002562603967701" style="display:none">This book has fallen victim to the “Loved the last book so I had high expectations” syndrome. I thought One of Us Is Lying was great, Two Can Keep a Secret was just okay.<br /><br />I expect these books to be cheesy – but this one was maybe too cheesy.<br /><br />The dialogue and the characters once again reminded me of a CW TV show. The blurb on the book does mention Riverdale and during the book one of the characters even mentions all the male actors on the CW. I think all of this combined felt like, “Look at me! I am like those shows! You have to like me because you like those shows! Lookie here! Uh . . . Supernatural! Did you hear me?? How about Pretty Little Liars!!! No, um, VAMPIRE DIARIES!!!! C’Mon! LOVE ME!”<br /><br />I expect these books to be mysterious – but this one maybe went a bit overboard.<br /><br />My wife described it best when we were done (we listened to the audiobook together in the evenings – a fun spouse activity if you have never tried it). She said that it felt like a series of thinly veiled mysteries piled on top of each other. Since there were so many they were trying to force together, it ended up being confusing and, in the end, when there was a resolution it was not all that satisfying because it was kind of hard to tell which mystery was being solved (and which parts were maybe just red herrings to throw us off).<br /><br />I expect these books to hold my interest – and this did . . . to a point.<br /><br />I have used the word “expect” a lot in this review. In general, it was what I expect from a YA mystery, there is no doubt about that. But, since it felt a bit like a forced followup to One Of Us is Lying, I found myself drifting at times. It didn’t feel particularly original in a genre that might be getting tougher and tougher to be original in. I will continue to give McManus a try since I have liked her work in the past and I have big hopes for the future, but this one was not really mu cup of tea.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14278002562603967701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1526243750255731679">Last year, I read <b>ONE OF US IS LYING</b> and loved it. It was a YA mystery/thriller by this author, so when I learned she was publishing a new book, I placed a hold on the library right away.<br/><br/>This is a <b>YA thriller/mystery</b> that takes place in the small town of Echo Ridge. The main narrator is Ellery, a high schooler who recently moved with her twin brother into their grandmother's house while their mom attends a rehab center for a few months.<br/><br/>Right from the start there's trouble, as Ellery and her brot</span>
  <span id="freeText1526243750255731679" style="display:none">Last year, I read <b>ONE OF US IS LYING</b> and loved it. It was a YA mystery/thriller by this author, so when I learned she was publishing a new book, I placed a hold on the library right away.<br /><br />This is a <b>YA thriller/mystery</b> that takes place in the small town of Echo Ridge. The main narrator is Ellery, a high schooler who recently moved with her twin brother into their grandmother's house while their mom attends a rehab center for a few months.<br /><br />Right from the start there's trouble, as Ellery and her brother arrive in town, along with their grandmother and a neighbor, they bump onto a dead body. It just gets <b>creepier and creepier</b> from then on.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book but not as much as <b>ONE OF US IS LYING</b>. It was a fun read, and I recommend it to readers of YA and contemporary fiction.</span>

  <span id="freeText12827733023994219242" style="display:none"><b> 4 stars! </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548053882ra/26949445.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Every single time I read the title of this book I had the PLL theme song running through my head.<br><br>Gotta say, McManus's sophmore novel knocked it out of the park! She is a officially an author I will be revisiting again and again in the future. If only she would write faster......<br><br>TCKAS is about twins Ellery and Ezra who move in with their grandmother after their mother goes into a care facility. Before they were born, their aunt had gone missing, about 5-6 years before another girl went missing. And not soon after the twins arrive in town threatening messages begin popping up everywhere leading the town to believe there's a killer ready to strike.<br><br>I really enjoyed this book, it was a great balance of teen soap (like a CW show) and a genuine mystery novel. I got some serious Riverdale and Pretty Little Liars vibes from this story and the characters. I honestly did not guess who did it, which I normally do. It may be obvious to other readers but I was stumped and that was a refreshing change for me.<br><br>I devoured this book, if you are on the fence I highly recommend giving it a try!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494101706i/22685352._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Follow me on ♥ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> ♥ <a href="http://rachelsreadsravenously.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ♥ <a href="http://instagram.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♥ <a href="https://twitter.com/rayliz89" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♥</span>

<div id="review_2645845994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2645845994" />
    <a title="Sophia Triad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44642860-sophia-triad"><img alt="Sophia Triad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591419108p2/44642860.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2645845994?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia Triad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia Triad" href="/user/show/44642860-sophia-triad">Sophia Triad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44642860-sophia-triad?shelf=crime-mafia">crime-mafia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44642860-sophia-triad?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2645845994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9925347346182594743"><b>Two can keep a secret...if one is dead.<br/>i.e. Two alive people could never keep a secret</b><br/><br/>Another absolutely fantastic book by the author of "One of Us is Lying"!<br/><br/>This is another book that confirms the truthfulness of the following rule: “NEVER start a new book, when you go to bed". You may not get any sleep. If it is a mystery book highly anticipated to read, you know that you will love it and you most probably stay up all night trying to solve the mystery and find who is the murderer before the las</span>
  <span id="freeText9925347346182594743" style="display:none"><b>Two can keep a secret...if one is dead.<br />i.e. Two alive people could never keep a secret</b><br /><br />Another absolutely fantastic book by the author of "One of Us is Lying"!<br /><br />This is another book that confirms the truthfulness of the following rule: “NEVER start a new book, when you go to bed". You may not get any sleep. If it is a mystery book highly anticipated to read, you know that you will love it and you most probably stay up all night trying to solve the mystery and find who is the murderer before the last chapter.<br /><br />Well, I never listen to advices anyway, I never learn....and I always repeat my previous mistakes. Maybe because they made me have fun.<br /><br />So, yes I stayed up all night reading and trying to discover the murderer of the two homecoming Queens from a small school in a small town in the middle of nowhere near a Halloween inspired theme park. The disappearance (murder???) of the first girl and the death of the second girl had many years difference and the murderer and his reasoning were never found out.<br /><br />Now there is a new school year, a new homecoming party and three new girls for the role of the new Queen. One of them is the niece of the first Queen who disappeared. Ellery and her twin brother Ezra are new in Echo Ridge. Their mother is in rehabilitation and the two teenagers will need to live with their grandmother.<br /><br />Ellery has a sharp mind and the attitude of an investigator.<br /><br />When strange things set in motion, <br />when scary threats are made to the girl who are nominees for the role of the Queen, <br />when one of them disappears <br /><b>Ellery will decide to investigate.</b><br /><br />The brother of the guy who is suspected for the murder of the second Queen will be her assistant, aka Malcolm. Nice and quite guy. He had never become the star athlete that his brother was in high school. And after the murder of the second girl, his family tried to lay as low as possible.<br /><br />The atmosphere of the book is mysterious (ha ha).<br />There are so many players to keep track of. And the story and the solution in the end are really complex.<br /><br />Let me just mentioned a few questions that kept popping up:<br /><b>1.	What happened to the first girl<br />2.	What happened to the second girl<br />3.	Is another girl going to disappear and who will that be<br />4.	Who killed the teacher <br />5.	Why Malcolm’s brother is back<br />6.	Who puts scary graffiti on the walls<br />7.	Who is Ellery and Ezra’s true father<br />8.	Why the post popular kids in school act so strangely <br />9.	Why the police investigator always so nervous around the twins<br />10.	What happened to Ellery's suitcase <br />11.	Why Ellery’s mother never talks about her sister<br />Etc. Etc. Etc.<br />And are all these events interconnected or they are random facts and events?</b><br /><br />The story has two points of view by Ellery and by Malcolm and the main events take place in just two months time.<br /><br />Highly recommended, just don't started before bedtime 😋</span>
  <a data-text-id="9925347346182594743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5603497290039877019">McManus does it again! Certainly no sophomore slump with Two Can Keep a Secret! I absolutely loved this story of a town with dark secrets that are seemingly resurfacing again. Twins Ezra and Ellery are staying with their Nana while their mother is doing a stint in rehab - however, they don’t know much about their mother’s hometown, where her twin sister was killed years before and when they move to the town and hear of other murders, they start asking questions, but what happens when they hear t</span>
  <span id="freeText5603497290039877019" style="display:none">McManus does it again! Certainly no sophomore slump with Two Can Keep a Secret! I absolutely loved this story of a town with dark secrets that are seemingly resurfacing again. Twins Ezra and Ellery are staying with their Nana while their mother is doing a stint in rehab - however, they don’t know much about their mother’s hometown, where her twin sister was killed years before and when they move to the town and hear of other murders, they start asking questions, but what happens when they hear the answers?<br /><br />Told in a suspenseful way that had me guessing and theorizing until the very last page, this book gave me everything I love from my YA books!<br /><br />Thank you to Random House Kids for an advance copy. All opinions are my own. </span>

<div id="review_2669964760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2669964760" />
    <a title="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13699205-ellias-elliasreads"><img alt="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580549084p2/13699205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2669964760?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" href="/user/show/13699205-ellias-elliasreads">ELLIAS (elliasreads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=thriller-mystery">thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=2019-books">2019-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2669964760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2579473569185976951"><i>
  <b>alright, alright, alright.....</b>
</i><br/><br/>This may come as a slight surprise to some folks who already know that I DNFed McManus' previous book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32571395.One_of_Us_Is_Lying' title='One of Us Is Lying by Karen M. McManus' rel='nofollow noopener'>One of Us Is Lying</a>, but I'm going to give this one a rating of <b>4 stars</b>. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>All three of them look like the kind of teenagers you'd find on a CW show—<u>too beautiful to read.</u></i>
</b><br/><br/>Literally, this whole quote encompasses everything I feel about this book. Think <i>Riverdale, Pretty Little Liars,</i> and even <i>The Vampire Diaries</i>. What do they have all in common? Pretty people i</span>
  <span id="freeText2579473569185976951" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>alright, alright, alright.....</b>
</i><br /><br />This may come as a slight surprise to some folks who already know that I DNFed McManus' previous book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32571395.One_of_Us_Is_Lying" title="One of Us Is Lying by Karen M. McManus" rel="nofollow noopener">One of Us Is Lying</a>, but I'm going to give this one a rating of <b>4 stars</b>. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>All three of them look like the kind of teenagers you'd find on a CW show—<u>too beautiful to read.</u></i>
</b><br /><br />Literally, this whole quote encompasses everything I feel about this book. Think <i>Riverdale, Pretty Little Liars,</i> and even <i>The Vampire Diaries</i>. What do they have all in common? Pretty people in the midst of tragedy and horror— a mysterious circumstance, a harrowing mystery itself, surviving amongst themselves and falling in love here and there. <br /><br />Not saying that that's whole book but then again,....it kinda was. I went into this book with very, <i>very</i>, and when I say very....I mean <b>hell of a very</b> low expectation. <br /><br />Thank god.<br /><br />I don't think I would have give this book the rating I did just now. It's somewhat slow and trudging, a quiet and ambivalent mystery set in a small town with a tragic past.....the usual trope most thrillers go by with a setting in a small town. <br /><br />However, <i>however</i>.....there were so many aspects I liked about this book that elevated the story from my rather 'low expectation' into something better, something more enjoyable, and surprising. <br /><br />1) Twins. <br />I really liked these two characters although I wish we had a main focus on the brother twin, Ezra, and not just the sister, Ellery, who had the main POV. <br /><br />2) Poking sentimental fun and knowing where it stands. <br />I think this book knows where it stands on a line of believability and realism. It pokes fun and calls back tropes of certain soapy high school TV, like the CW, mean girls 'wearing pink on Wednesday. It knows <i>exactly</i> what it is and I respect that. <br /><br />3) The last 10 pages. <br />I would have given this book a 3 star rating if it hadn't been for those last ten pages. The book itself didn't bring anything new to the table; but there was such a monstrosity of surprise out of nowhere I was completely delighted to find that I enjoyed it immensely. The ending was somewhat rushed and I wish it could have expanded juuuuuust a bit.....but that very ending.....<i>wow</i>. <br /><br />What I didn't like: <br /><br />1) Romance. <br /><i>UGH</i>. Of course. Not really great and could have skipped it altogether. <br /><br />2) Not enough thrills or tension. <br /><br />3) Small towns with too many blonde-hair and blue-eyed people scare me more than Michael Myers or Freddy Krueger......pretty sure they were white too but the point is, there are some diverse characters sprinkled here and there. But then again, they either don't do much or get sidelined. Actually come to think of it, most YA books are better with representing diverse and queer characters more than the actual adult thrillers I usually read. <br /><br /><b>Holy shit</b> this review is looooong wtf I was not expecting to write this much or be as critical LOL. <br /><br />Honestly, if you're looking for something thrilling and fast paced, I'm not too sure this might be the book for you. It's rather unremarkable in terms of the small town mystery so many other books have done before and rather slow and unprecedented in it's mystery and pacing <i>but</i>........<br /><br />I think if you go into this one without expecting much, the outcome will be much, much greater, with happier and better results. <b>
  <i>Perfect</i>
</b> for anyone looking to try out the genre though. Definite recommend if you're looking for that. <br /><a href="https://twitter.com/elliasreads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/elliasreads/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookstagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/ellias" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> |</span>
  <a data-text-id="2579473569185976951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2653047467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13837501131558212036">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“You know what they say. When in Murderland . . .”</i>
</b><br/><br/>After practically crapping my pants over <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918742423?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>One Of Us Is Lying</a>, I wanted this in my life as soon as I saw it on NetGalley . . . and was immediately denied my request, naturally. Luckily, I have the most awesome of libraries to provide a hook-up. <br/><br/><i>Two Can Keep A Secret</i> is told from Ellery’s perspective. She and her twin brother Ezra have been relocated to their Granny’s house after their</span>
  <span id="freeText13837501131558212036" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“You know what they say. When in Murderland . . .”</i>
</b><br><br>After practically crapping my pants over <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918742423?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">One Of Us Is Lying</a>, I wanted this in my life as soon as I saw it on NetGalley . . . and was immediately denied my request, naturally. Luckily, I have the most awesome of libraries to provide a hook-up. <br><br><i>Two Can Keep A Secret</i> is told from Ellery’s perspective. She and her twin brother Ezra have been relocated to their Granny’s house after their mother had a bit of a run-in with a plate glass window while driving . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551110854ra/27116611.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Granny’s location? Echo Ridge. A town known for disappearing girls. The first was Ellery’s aunt (and mother’s twin sister) back in the day. Another five years ago. And now???? It appears to be starting all over and once again it appears one of the homecoming princesses may be the target . . . . .<br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551110854ra/27116612.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Lemme tell you Karen McManus knows what the eff she’s doing when it comes to teenie-bopper mysteries. As a grown-up (a/k/a not target demographic) as well as an avid mystery reader, I will note that before page 50 I had made a notation that “REDACTED did it.” I’m also telling you . . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551110854ra/27116613.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This was so much fun. <br><br>And as an old lady, let’s discuss this cover. Once again, MAAAAAADDDDDDDDDDD props to authors who are bright enough to have similar covers. If someone name-dropped Karen McManus randomly, I am 100% certain I’d be all “who?” Buuuuuuuut, thanks to this cover looking remarkably similar to her first YA mystery release, I was all over wanting to read it like stink on a poo poo platter. (Bonus this time with the “One” then “Two” titling. Will a Three be next???? I hope so!) <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13837501131558212036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText7674434172604445736" style="display:none">I enjoyed the mystery part of this one a lot more than I did <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2101553026" rel="nofollow noopener">One of Us Is Lying</a>. Then there's a little extra <i>twist</i> thing at the end. &lt;--but to be honest, that didn't surprise me at all. <br>Still.<br><b>IT'S YA <i>and I don't wanna be too judgy.</i></b><br><br>So. Actress Twin ends up in rehab and <i>her</i> twins end up going to live in the town she grew up in with grandma. In the meantime, another pretty prom queen has been killed and her killer never found.<br><i>Dun, dun, duuuun.</i><br>The kids show up in Echo Ridge and right away there's a hit and run that kills a universally beloved teacher, some threatening graffiti and creepy dolls, and a lot of angst. Most of it because young girl-twin (Ellery) is an amateur crime...watcher? I don't know what to call it. Yes, unbelievably, they don't run around telling teen sleuths confidential information that pertains to murder cases. <br>I know!     <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2423002700?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/44463467-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44463467-nina?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44463467-nina?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2423002700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3589041577628210684"><b>*Thanks again to Penguin Random House for sending me an ARC of this book via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.* </b><br/><br/>Last Christmas, I read One Of Us Is Lying and I really enjoyed it, so I was very excited about getting an ARC of this book and thus being able to spend another Christmas reading one of Karen M. McManus's novels. <br/><br/>Just like Karen's first book, Two Can Keep a Secret was a very quick read and I really enjoyed it. I'm still absolutely in love with her writing style because she jus</span>
  <span id="freeText3589041577628210684" style="display:none"><b>*Thanks again to Penguin Random House for sending me an ARC of this book via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.* </b><br /><br />Last Christmas, I read One Of Us Is Lying and I really enjoyed it, so I was very excited about getting an ARC of this book and thus being able to spend another Christmas reading one of Karen M. McManus's novels. <br /><br />Just like Karen's first book, Two Can Keep a Secret was a very quick read and I really enjoyed it. I'm still absolutely in love with her writing style because she just has a way of drawing you in and glueing you to the book. But while Two Can Keep a Secret was another very gripping novel by her, I have to say that it just wasn't as suspenseful as One Of Us Is Lying was. That book just left me guessing a little more and almost till the very end, I didn't really know how everything would be wrapped up. This time around, it was definitely a little easier to guess what had happened. <br /><br />However, one thing I really loved about this book was the cast of characters even though I wish that Ezra and Mia had gotten a little bit more screen time. Also, I sometimes mention great first sentences in my reviews of books but Two Can Keep a Secret had an amazing last sentence instead!<br /><br />So all in all, Two Can Keep a Secret is definitely a 2019 release you should check out. It's a great mystery novel with a gripping plot that one can easily read in one sitting and I definitely don't regret that I preordered a final copy of this several months ago.<br /><br /><b><a href="http://www.instagram.com/theenchantingbooks" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a> || <a href="http://www.theenchantingbooks.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a> || <a href="https://www.twitter.com/nina_lemb" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> </b></span>
